вқҜ Urme V2 вҖ” Plan                                                                
  1. Schema                                                                     
  SQLite tables:                                                                
                                                                                
  steps вҖ” one row per promptвҶ’response turn, structured metadata                 
  steps_fts вҖ” FTS5 virtual table over summary, tags, prompt_text (porter        
  stemmer)                                                                      
  entities вҖ” named concepts, files, decisions, bugs, patterns                   
  relationships вҖ” edges between entities, with step_id provenance               
  sessions вҖ” metadata about each Claude Code session                            
                                                                                
  Drop: sqlite-vec, embeddings entirely                                         
                                                                                
  2. Indexing Pipeline                                                          
  When a session is processed:                                                  
                                                                                
  Parse stream-json вҶ’ extract turns                                             
  For each turn:                                                                
                                                                                
  Extract structured metadata deterministically (files, commands, tokens,       
  timestamps)                                                                   
  Correlate with git walk (commit_before/after, human edits)                    
  Call Claude: generate summary + tags + extract entities/relationships         
  Deduplicate entities against existing graph (Claude compares against current  
  entity list)                                                                  
  Write step to SQLite + FTS5                                                   
  Write new/merged entities and relationships to graph tables                   
                                                                                
                                                                                
  Human edits from git walk вҶ’ stored as steps with session_id = NULL            
                                                                                
                                                                                
  3. Search Pipeline                                                            
                                                                                
  User enters natural language query in TUI                                     
  Load graph from SQLite into OCamlGraph (fresh, fast)                          
  Entity resolution: Claude checks if query mentions known entities вҶ’ direct    
  graph lookup if so                                                            
  FTS5 query generation: Claude produces structured JSON:                       
                                                                                
  json   {                                                                      
       "queries": ["taint propagator ocaml", "taint analysis dataflow"],        
       "repo": "opengrep",                                                      
       "after": null,                                                           
       "has_commit": null                                                       
     }                                                                          
                                                                                
  Execute SQL combining FTS5 MATCH + WHERE filters, fallback through query      
  alternatives                                                                  
  Graph traversal: for matched steps, fetch related entities via OCamlGraph     
  (1-2 hops)                                                                    
  Claude re-ranking: pass shortlist + subgraph context, get ranked results +    
  synthesis                                                                     
  Write back: Claude notes any new connections discovered вҶ’ written to graph    
  Display in TUI                                                                
                                                                                
                                                                                
  4. OCaml Module Structure                                                     
  urme/                                                                         
    bin/                                                                        
      main.ml          -- CLI entry, dispatch                                   
    lib/                                                                        
      schema.ml        -- SQLite schema, migrations                             
      indexer.ml       -- stream-json parsing, git correlation                  
      graph.ml         -- OCamlGraph wrapper, load/traverse                     
      claude.ml        -- all Claude calls (summarise, search, deduplicate)     
      search.ml        -- search pipeline orchestration                         
      fts.ml           -- FTS5 query construction                               
      tui.ml           -- terminal UI                                           
                                                                                
  5. Claude Call Inventory                                                      
  WhenPurposeSizeIndex time, per stepSummary + tags + entity                    
  extractionMediumIndex time, per sessionEntity deduplication against           
  graphSmallSearch timeFTS5 query generationTinySearch timeRe-rank shortlist +  
  synthesisMediumSearch timeWrite back new edgesTiny                            
                                                                                
  6. Build Order                                                                
                                                                                
  Schema + migrations                                                           
  Stream-json parser + git correlation (mostly exists)                          
  Claude summarisation + FTS5 indexing (new core)                               
  Basic search вҖ” FTS5 only, no graph yet                                        
  Entity extraction + graph storage                                             
  Graph-aware search + OCamlGraph traversal                                     
  Claude re-ranking + write-back                                                
  Export/import utility                                                         
  TUI polish                                                                    
                                                                                
                                                                                
  7. Deferred                                                                   
                                                                                
  Multi-machine merge                                                           
  Daemon mode                                                                   
  Human edit summarisation (store but don't summarise initially)

вҸә Review / Critique

  Read through the plan and the existing code. The direction is sound вҖ” drop the
   ChromaDB/Ollama embeddings stack, move to SQLite+FTS5+graph, keep
  git_walk/diff_match as-is. Critiques, ordered by load-bearingness:

  1. Two serial Claude calls per search is expensive. Query вҶ’ Claude (FTS
  rewrite) вҶ’ SQL вҶ’ Claude (rerank) means every "вҶ‘ enter" in the TUI waits on two
   LLM round-trips. The first rewrite is often unnecessary вҖ” most queries
  tokenize fine as direct FTS5 MATCH. Suggest: skip Claude on step 4, go
  straight to FTS5 with the user's tokens; only call Claude for a rewrite if the
   hit count is 0 or obviously poor. Cuts median search latency ~50%.

  2. Entity deduplication at index time doesn't scale. "Claude compares against
  current entity list" вҖ” at 10k entities that prompt gets huge. Pre-filter
  locally (trigram similarity on name/aliases, cap at ~30 candidates), only then
   ask Claude. Otherwise indexing cost grows linearly with graph size.

  3. Load graph fresh on every search is fine until it isn't. OK at вүӨ5k edges;
  painful past that. Cheap fix: keep an in-memory Graph.t in the TUI process
  with a graph_version integer in SQLite вҖ” only reload when it bumps.

  4. Write-back during search is a feedback loop + concurrency risk. Query
  shapes graph shapes next query, and if urme serve runs the MCP handlers
  concurrently with the TUI, both will try to write edges. Gate write-back
  behind a confidence threshold, and turn on SQLite WAL mode from day one.

  5. Human edits as session_id = NULL steps invisible to search. FTS5 indexes
  summary, tags, prompt_text; human steps have none of those. Section 7 defers
  their summarisation, which means until then they can only be found by exact
  file/commit filters. Fine as a deliberate deferral but worth calling out.

  6. Batch summarisation. A 500-turn session = 500 Claude calls at index time.
  Batch 5вҖ“10 consecutive turns per call (share prompt cache), or summarise
  lazily on first search. Not a blocker for step 3, but decide before scaling.

  7. Missing from plan:
  - Migration story from existing ChromaDB вҖ” assume wipe & reindex? (probably
  yes; say so.)
  - Concurrency: WAL mode, single writer assumption, what happens when MCP + TUI
   + indexer all run.
  - Schema specifics: is tags a comma string in FTS5 or a separate table? What
  relationship types are allowed?

  8. Build order вҖ” one swap. Move step 8 (export/import) before step 5 (entity
  extraction). Once you have FTS5 steps working you can already dogfood; having
  import/export early makes it trivial to reset & replay during graph work.

  None of these are blockers. The shape is right.

  Now saving the plan and starting on step 1.

вқҜ really? ugh ... is chromadb inappropiate then?                                

вҸә No, Chroma isn't inappropriate вҖ” it's just more machinery than you might need.
   The honest tradeoff:

  What Chroma gives you that FTS5 doesn't:
  - Semantic match вҖ” finds "JWT discussion" when the query says "auth", even if
  the word "auth" never appears. For free-form chat logs this genuinely helps.

  What Chroma costs you:
  - Separate server process + Ollama embedding service вҶ’ port management,
  auto-start logic, more moving parts.
  - Can't do structured SQL filters (after date, repo, has_commit) natively вҖ”
  has to go through metadata filters which are awkward.
  - You already hit UTF-8 sanitisation bugs against it (per memory). Operational
   scar tissue.
  - If V2 adds entities/relationships anyway, you'll need a relational store
  regardless вҖ” so it's Chroma plus SQLite, not Chroma vs. SQLite.

  The V2 bet is: "Claude-rewritten FTS5 + entity graph reaches the same recall
  as embeddings, without the ops burden." Plausible for your domain (code +
  conversations where exact file/function names matter a lot), but not a slam
  dunk.

  Middle path worth considering: keep SQLite as the source of truth for
  steps/entities/graph, use FTS5 as the default search, and leave Chroma in
  place only as a semantic fallback when FTS5 returns 0 hits. You'd still lose
  the ops headache eventually but not on day one.

  Want me to (a) stick with the full drop-Chroma plan, (b) take the middle path,
   or (c) pause and keep Chroma, just add the graph side?

вқҜ yes let's gp                                                                  
вҸә Proceeding with the full drop-Chroma V2 plan. Writing db.ml and schema.ml.

вқҜ ok so now is the Chromedb gone?                                               

  Searched for 2 patterns (ctrl+o to expand)

вҸә No вҖ” ChromaDB is still very much present. What I built is parallel, not a
  replacement yet. Honest picture:

  Still depends on ChromaDB (build and/or runtime):
  - lib/search/chromadb.ml вҖ” the client itself, still compiled into urme_search
  - lib/mcp/handlers.ml вҖ” all 6 MCP tools (urme serve) call it
  - lib/engine/{git_index,git_link,walk_handlers}.ml вҖ” the old git-link engine
  reads/writes interaction metadata through it
  - lib/tui/app.ml вҖ” still wired to it
  - lib/core/config.ml вҖ” chromadb_port field, default 8000
  - bin/main.ml вҖ” --chromadb-port flag passed to all subcommands (unused by my
  new ones)
  - scripts/start.sh, scripts/setup.sh вҖ” still install and launch it
  - README.md вҖ” still documents it

  New V2 pipeline (SQLite only, no Chroma):
  - urme init вҶ’ indexes JSONL вҶ’ SQLite + FTS5, runs Claude summarisation
  - urme search вҶ’ FTS5 BM25 only
  - The .urme/db.sqlite store is independent; you can run it with ChromaDB
  turned off

  So today they coexist. The plan (В§4, В§7) always deferred actual deletion вҖ” the
   module layout note says "lib/search/chromadb.ml вҖ” deleted once search.ml is 
  the default", meaning after the TUI (task #9) stops calling Chroma.

  Options:
  1. Keep going through task #5/6/7/8 (export/import вҶ’ entities вҶ’ graph вҶ’
  rerank), then cut Chroma out in one final sweep as part of task #9. This is
  what the plan says.
  2. Cut Chroma now. Rip out chromadb.ml, rewrite mcp/handlers.ml on top of
  Search.run, delete chromadb_port from config/CLI, gut the install scripts.
  This is probably a full session of work on its own вҖ” MCP has 6 tools all
  Chroma-backed, and the old git-link engine uses Chroma as its metadata store,
  so we'd need to either rewrite those against SQLite or just delete them.
  3. Partial cut now. Stop building Chroma (remove from urme_search deps), keep
  the file around but orphaned. Fastest way to know what actually depends on it
  вҖ” the compiler will tell us.

  My recommendation: option 1. The V2 pipeline works in isolation; ripping
  Chroma out is a lot of churn and the graph work in task #6-8 doesn't need it
  gone. Do it once at the end when we know what the new TUI + MCP look like.

  Which do you want?

  вҺҝ В    turn_index = 0
            prompt = SO I have a serious problem with the trst, seems to ha
     ve an issue with "new files"
     вҖҰ +72 lines (ctrl+o to expand)

вҸә Genuinely good. Quick evaluation across the 12 sampled turns:

  Strengths:
  - Concrete identifiers preserved вҖ” diff_match.ml, split_into_turns, commit
  305207d, test_engine.exe, specific numbers like "500 to 2000 chars", "77 PASS,
   0 FAIL, 44 SKIP". This is exactly what lexical search needs; FTS5 will find a
   turn by any of those exact tokens.
  - Problem-solution pairing вҖ” summaries describe both the issue and the fix,
  e.g. "Fixed 4 test failures in diff_match.ml by detecting renamed files via 
  git diff-tree -M10 and using old path's content as content_before".
  Self-contained; you don't need to read the prompt.
  - Handles sparse prompts well вҖ” turn 7 ("can you run it") gets the action
  summary, not an echo of the prompt. Turn 2 ("but some links i get are empty")
  correctly ties back to the prior fixes.
  - Tags are an orthogonal hook вҖ” content_before, rename-detection, off-by-one,
  turn_idx, p5-miss, chromadb-persistence. Technical nouns Claude wouldn't have
  written in a prose summary.
  - Length compliance вҖ” everything is one sentence, most under 30 words.

  Minor gripes (none are blockers):
  - Hyphenated tags like rename-detection get split by FTS5's unicode61 
  tokenizer вҖ” they index as two tokens (rename, detection). Searches for either
  word hit; searches for the exact compound as a phrase don't. Usually fine,
  occasionally surprising.
  - Tags sometimes redundant with files_touched вҖ” e.g. chromadb.ml app.ml appear
   both in tags and in the files_touched JSON. Wasted tag budget but harmless.
  - Turn 5 is the weakest вҖ” it was a meta-turn (task-notification paste), and
  the summary says what was summarised rather than the substance of those
  summaries. Marginal turns will always be marginal.
  - Turn 3 softens specifics вҖ” "found no matching interactions indexed" is a bit
   generic; the concrete failure mode is lost. Tags salvage it.

  Bottom line: these summaries will give you much better search recall than raw
  prompt_text alone, and noticeably better precision than an embedding-only
  approach вҖ” because the high-signal identifiers (function names, file paths,
  commit shas) are surfaced as searchable tokens. The tag layer is the
  underrated part вҖ” it's doing real work above and beyond the prose.

  Want me to re-check progress, or press on to task #5 (export/import) once
  summarisation finishes?

вҸә Summary of what you can ask the DB right now:

  - Lexical search with BM25: steps_fts MATCH 'taint propagator', 'human edits',
   etc. Works across summary + tags + prompt_text. Scores are negative; closer
  to 0 = less relevant.
  - File-scoped history: "every turn that touched app.ml" via
  json_each(files_touched). 80 hits for app.ml вҖ” that's where most of the churn
  lives.
  - Command-scoped history: who ran dune build variants вҖ” 99+ runs across 3
  truncated variants.
  - Timeline queries: WHERE timestamp BETWEEN x AND y or WHERE commit_after = 
  'b370fda' uses the indexed column.
  - Cross-session: group by session_id; session bf332f06 (Mar 16, 198 turns) is
  by far the biggest.
  - Token stats (with caveat): tokens_in here is incremental new-message tokens
  per turn (~13 avg), so don't read it as full context cost вҖ” cached prior
  tokens aren't counted. tokens_out is real output.
  - Git coverage: 391/391 have commit_before, 305/391 have commit_after (the 86
  most-recent turns have no subsequent commit yet).

  What's missing, so you can't ask yet:
  - Entity queries вҖ” entities and relationships tables are empty (task #6).
  - Semantic match (non-lexical) вҖ” you'd need to search around key terms rather
  than concepts. Task #8 (Claude rerank) would help.
  - Human-edit rows вҖ” not populated (section В§7 deferred).

  Want me to resume task #5 (round-trip test using a copy of the live DB, not
  touching it), or pivot somewhere else?

вҸә Apples-to-apples comparison for the same three turns. Important finding first:
   Chroma isn't storing "Ollama summaries" вҖ” it's storing raw concatenated User:
   ... + Files: ... + assistant text blocks as the embedding source. There's no
  LLM distillation on the Chroma side, Ollama was used only for the embedding
  (turning that text into a vector). So this is "raw extract for semantic
  embedding" vs "Claude-compressed lexical index":

  Turn 0 вҖ” "serious problem with the trst..."

  narration ("Let me look... Let me run... Found it... All 4 failures are new 
  files...")
  - V2 summary (~130 chars): "Fixed 4 test failures in diff_match.ml by 
  detecting renamed files via git diff-tree -M10 and using old path's content as
   content_before."
  - V2 tags: diff_match rename-detection test_engine git-diff-tree 
  content_before ocaml

  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ Semantic fuzzy match   в”Ӯ yes (via embedding)       в”Ӯ no                в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ Exact identifier       в”Ӯ inconsistent (buried in   в”Ӯ concentrated in   в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ tokens                 в”Ӯ prose)                    в”Ӯ tags              в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ BM25 lexical precision в”Ӯ diluted by prose          в”Ӯ very high         в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ Scannable in search    в”Ӯ no                        в”Ӯ yes               в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ results                в”Ӯ                           в”Ӯ                   в”Ӯ
  в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

  Takeaway: the V2 summaries are ~6Г— smaller and have much higher token density
  of useful identifiers (the 30-odd words are nearly all signal). They'll
  outperform Chroma documents on lexical queries because BM25 weights rare terms
   more when the doc is short. Chroma's docs are better if you want to read what
   Claude actually explained вҖ” but you get that by reading the JSONL anyway.

  So the two approaches are mostly complementary, not competing: V2 summary =
  "what was done"; Chroma doc = "the reasoning". If you ever wanted both, you'd
  keep the JSONL pointer + V2 summary (which you already do via session_id +
  turn_index). No need for Ollama in the loop.

  Want me to also pull a later turn (say turn 50+) where Chroma's document
  format might differ, or move on?

вҸә Now we're comparing real behaviour. Three queries, three very different
  stories:

  Query 1: "why did tests fail on new files"
  - Chroma nails it: top hit is turn 0 вҖ” "serious problem with the trst, seems 
  to have an issue with 'new files'" (the exact user prompt).
  - V2 returns adjacent "test passes" turns but misses turn 0. My summary for
  turn 0 rewrote "new files" as "test failures in diff_match.ml", dropping the
  literal phrase вҖ” so FTS5 can't match it.
  - Chroma wins on this one. Lesson: when the user remembers the literal
  phrasing, semantic embedding that preserves raw text beats a compressed
  summary.

  Query 2: "how did we detect human edits"
  - V2 top hit is "Agreed to add human edit detection via leftover unexplained 
  content after Claude edit undo, adding human_edits hashtable to update_index 
  in git_link.ml." вҖ” that is the turn answering the question.
  - Chroma top hits are two junk rows ([human edit] Makefile) вҖ” those are
  human-edit placeholders with no content. The actual user-phrased turn is 3rd.
  - V2 wins вҖ” precision (position 1 is on point, not position 3). Also V2
  returned the answer; Chroma returned only the question.

  Query 3: "what caused the TUI to freeze"
  - V2 top hit: "Diagnosed and fixed Lwt_mvar deadlock in switch_to_gitвҖҰ 
  freezing TUI input." вҖ” bullseye.
  - Chroma: "now?", "but what aout teadme?", "but why? is Irvin not able to do 
  the right thing?" вҖ” completely useless. The embedding pulled short
  frustrated-user turns that happen to cluster near the query vector in
  embedding space.
  - V2 wins overwhelmingly.

  Pattern:

  в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
  в”Ӯ      Query kind      в”Ӯ Winner в”Ӯ                   Why                   в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө

  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ Generic verb         в”Ӯ V2     в”Ӯ semantic embedding degrades hard on     в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ ("freeze", "crash")  в”Ӯ        в”Ӯ low-signal queries                      в”Ӯ
  в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

  Upshot for V2 design: query 1's miss is the only real red flag вҖ” and it's a
  fixable one. The prompt_text column is FTS-indexed, but V2 summaries are
  winning the BM25 race over raw prompts because they're shorter and higher
  density. Consider: weight prompt_text less in bm25 (via bm25(steps_fts, 1.0, 
  1.0, 0.3)) so rare user-phrase tokens still surface. Or: keep the current
  setup; add a "grep prompt_text" mode as a secondary search. This is exactly
  the kind of thing the Claude-rewrite path (task #8) is meant to fix вҖ”
  rewriting "new files" into "diff_match.ml new files" before the MATCH.

  Bottom line: V2 wins the real use cases (2 of 3), and the one Chroma wins is
  recoverable. Drop Ollama.

          +pt: %s"                                                       
      223 +      c.step_id c.turn_index                                  
      224 +      (clamp 200 c.summary)                                   
      225 +      (clamp 120 c.tags)                                      
      226 +      (clamp 120 c.prompt_excerpt)                            
      227 +  ) candidates in                                             
      228 +  String.concat "\n" [                                        
      229 +    "You rerank search results for a coding-session history da
          +tabase.";                                                     
      230 +    "";                                                       
      231 +    "User query: " ^ Printf.sprintf "%S" query;               
      232 +    "";                                                       
      233 +    "Candidate rows (unsorted):";                             
      234 +    String.concat "\n" rows;                                  
      235 +    "";                                                       
      236 +    "Return a JSON object with two keys:";                    
      237 +    "- `ranked`: array of step_id integers, best first, only f
          +rom the \                                                     
      238 +     candidates above. Drop ones that clearly don't match.";  
      239 +    "- `synthesis`: ONE short sentence answering the user's qu
          +estion, \                                                     
      240 +     grounded in the kept rows. Empty string if the candidates
          + don't \                                                      
      241 +     answer it.";                                             
      242 +    "";                                                       
      243 +    "Output ONLY the JSON object. No prose, no fences.";      
      244 +  ]                                                           
      245 +                                                              
      246 +let parse_rerank_response raw : rerank_output =               
      247 +  match Yojson.Safe.from_string raw with                      
      248 +  | exception _ -> { ranked_step_ids = []; synthesis = "" }   
      249 +  | json ->                                                   
      250 +    let open Yojson.Safe.Util in                              
      251 +    let ranked =                                              
      252 +      match json |> member "ranked" with                      
      253 +      | `List xs ->                                           
      254 +        List.filter_map (fun j -> try Some (to_int j) with _ -
          +> None) xs                                                    
      255 +      | _ -> []                                               
      256 +    in                                                        
      257 +    let synthesis =                                           
      258 +      json |> member "synthesis" |> to_string_option          
      259 +      |> Option.value ~default:""                             
      260 +    in                                                        
      261 +    { ranked_step_ids = ranked; synthesis }                   
      262 +                                                              
      263 +let rerank ~binary ~query ~(candidates : rerank_input list) = 
      264 +  match candidates with                                       
      265 +  | [] -> Lwt.return { ranked_step_ids = []; synthesis = "" } 
      266 +  | _ ->                                                      
      267 +    let prompt = build_rerank_prompt ~query ~candidates in    
      268 +    let* raw = ask ~binary ~prompt in                         
      269 +    Lwt.return (parse_rerank_response raw)

       66      let widened = run ~db ~limit ~join:Or query in

       72 +(* Deduplicate by step_id, preserving the order of first occur

       73 +let dedup_by_id hits =                                        
       74 +  let seen = Hashtbl.create 16 in                             
       75 +  List.filter (fun (h : hit) ->                               
       76 +    if Hashtbl.mem seen h.step_id then false                  
       77 +    else (Hashtbl.add seen h.step_id (); true)                
       78 +  ) hits                                                      
       79 +                                                              
       80 +(* If the initial FTS5 pass is sparse (< [~min_hits_for_fast])
          +, ask Claude                                                  
       81 +   for alternative phrasings and union their hits. Returns the
          + merged hit                                                   
       82 +   list with duplicates dropped. *)                           
       83 +let expand_with_rewrite                                       
       84 +    ~db ~binary ?(limit=default_limit) ?(min_hits_for_fast=3) 
          +query =                                                       
       85 +  let open Lwt.Syntax in                                      
       86 +  let primary = run_with_fallback ~db ~limit query in         
       87 +  if List.length primary >= min_hits_for_fast then Lwt.return 
          +primary                                                       
       88 +  else                                                        
       89 +    let weak_summaries =                                      
       90 +      List.map (fun (h : hit) -> h.summary) primary           
       91 +      |> List.filter (fun s -> s <> "")                       
       92 +      |> (fun xs -> if List.length xs > 5                     
       93 +           then List.filteri (fun i _ -> i < 5) xs            
       94 +           else xs)

       96 +    let* alts = Urme_claude.Prompts.rewrite_query ~binary

       99 +    let extra = List.concat_map (fun q ->                     
      100 +      run ~db ~limit ~join:And q                              
      101 +    ) alts in                                                 
      102 +    Lwt.return (dedup_by_id (primary @ extra))                
      103 +                                                              
      104 +(* Bundle FTS5 expansion + Claude rerank + synthesis. Returns 
          +(ordered                                                      
      105 +   hits, synthesis). Ordering follows Claude's ranked step_ids
          +; hits                                                        
      106 +   Claude didn't rank get appended at the end by original BM25
          +. *)                                                          
      107 +let run_smart                                                 
      108 +    ~db ~binary                                               
      109 +    ?(limit=default_limit)                                    
      110 +    ?(shortlist_size=12)                                      
      111 +    query =                                                   
      112 +  let open Lwt.Syntax in                                      
      113 +  let* candidates = expand_with_rewrite ~db ~binary           
      114 +      ~limit:(max limit shortlist_size) query in              
      115 +  let shortlist =                                             
      116 +    if List.length candidates <= shortlist_size then candidate
          +s                                                             
      117 +    else List.filteri (fun i _ -> i < shortlist_size) candidat
          +es                                                            
      118 +  in                                                          
      119 +  let inputs = List.map (fun (h : hit) ->                     
      120 +    { Urme_claude.Prompts.step_id = h.step_id;                
      121 +      turn_index = h.turn_index;                              
      122 +      summary = h.summary;                                    
      123 +      tags = h.tags;                                          
      124 +      prompt_excerpt =                                        
      125 +        if String.length h.prompt_text > 160                  
      126 +        then String.sub h.prompt_text 0 160 ^ "..."           
      127 +        else h.prompt_text }                                  
      128 +  ) shortlist in                                              
      129 +  let* { ranked_step_ids; synthesis } =                       
      130 +    Urme_claude.Prompts.rerank ~binary ~query ~candidates:inpu
          +ts in                                                         
      131 +  let by_id = Hashtbl.create (List.length candidates) in      
      132 +  List.iter (fun (h : hit) -> Hashtbl.add by_id h.step_id h) c
          +andidates;                                                    
      133 +  let ranked =                                                
      134 +    List.filter_map (fun id -> Hashtbl.find_opt by_id id) rank
          +ed_step_ids in                                                
      135 +  let ranked_set = List.fold_left (fun acc id -> id :: acc) []
      136 +      ranked_step_ids in                                      
      137 +  let tail = List.filter (fun (h : hit) ->                    
      138 +    not (List.mem h.step_id ranked_set)) candidates in        
      139 +  let final = ranked @ tail in                                
      140 +  let cut =                                                   
      141 +    if List.length final <= limit then final                  
      142 +    else List.filteri (fun i _ -> i < limit) final            
      143 +  in                                                          
      144 +  Lwt.return (cut, synthesis)

вқҜ wait a bit the gt walk handlers git_index etc are needeed to connect to git   
  no?                                                                           

вҸә Good pause вҖ” let me explain clearly what's git-connective vs. what was Chroma
  glue. I was precise about which 3 files I deleted:

  Still here, still working (git-connective):
  - lib/git/ops.ml вҖ” every git subprocess call (git log, git diff, git blame,
  git rev-parse, вҖҰ). Untouched.
  - lib/store/project_store.ml вҖ” Irmin-git repo access. Untouched.
  - lib/engine/git_walk.ml вҖ” the pure branch-folding algorithm (EditGroup/Commit
   events вҶ’ file_state transitions + human-edit reconciliation). Kept.
  - lib/engine/diff_match.ml вҖ” per-commit diff decomposition into Claude-edit
  provenance. Kept.
  - lib/engine/edit_extract.ml вҖ” pulls Edit/Write tool_use blocks out of JSONL
  into edit records. Kept.
  - lib/engine/branch_topo.ml вҖ” labels commits with branches. Kept.
  - lib/engine/git_link_types.ml вҖ” shared types. Kept.
  - lib/engine/indexer.ml (V2) вҖ” runs git log per session branch and stamps each
   turn with commit_before/commit_after. New, wired in.

  The three I deleted were specifically Chroma glue, not git:
  - git_index.ml вҖ” orchestrator that ran Git_walk.walk with a Chroma-writing 
  handler to populate Chroma with per-edit git_info metadata. The whole purpose
  of that file was writing to Chroma.
  - walk_handlers.ml вҖ” the Chroma-writing handler implementation
  (materialise/save callbacks that stored into Chroma).
  - git_link.ml вҖ” MCP's file_history / region_history which read per-edit
  linkage back from Chroma.

  What we actually lost (capability, not git access):
  1. Per-edit commit linkage вҖ” which specific Edit tool_use inside turn X caused
   which hunk in commit Y. V2 is turn-level only (one step row per turn, one
  commit_before/after pair).
  2. Reconciliation-based human-edit detection вҖ” when a commit has content no
  Claude edit explains, git_walk attributed it to a human. V2 doesn't do this
  yet; human-edit rows are in plan В§7 deferred.
  3. Fine-grained MCP responses вҖ” file_history / region_blame used to return
  per-edit provenance; they now return step-level rows.

  Git itself is fully connected. The "link keys" count you'll see in the Git
  browser header is now sourced from the V2 SQLite store: each (commit_sha, 
  file_basename) pair with a step that touched that file at that commit.

  Options from here:
  - (a) Proceed with the wean-off вҖ” accept the feature loss for now, add
  per-edit linkage back later when the graph work unparks. Exactly what the
  original plan В§7 deferred.
  - (b) Revert the three deletions (I still have them in git history). Keep
  walk_handlers.ml / git_index.ml / git_link.ml around but stub out the Chroma 
  writes so they compile without the client вҖ” leaves the analysis scaffolding
  and human-edit reconciliation in place, just without a sink. Requires rewiring
   them to write to SQLite, which is a real chunk of work.
  - (c) Restore them as-is for reference only, move to a deprecated/
  subdirectory, exclude from the build. Keeps the algorithm visible but out of
  the way.

  Which path?

вҸә Now the big one вҖ” git_link.ml. Let me first scan what its signatures expose.

  Searched for 2 patterns, read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

вҸә Good вҖ” file_history and region_history don't actually use Chroma at all, they
  call Diff_match (pure). The Chroma usage was entirely inside update_index,
  which is superseded by the cleaner Git_index.update I just rewrote. Stripping
  git_link.ml to just the two MCP-facing functions.

вҸә Bash(dune build 2>&1 | head -30)
  вҺҝ В (No output)

вҸә Yes вҖ” summarisation is exactly the kind of task Haiku 4.5 is built for:
  structured extraction from a bounded input, no multi-step reasoning needed.
  It'll be ~3Г— cheaper and ~2Г— faster with essentially the same output quality.
  The rewrite-query + rerank paths I'd keep on the default model (benefit from
  better reasoning), but summarisation can absolutely go to Haiku.

  Wiring it now.

вҸә Write(README.md)

        1 -# Experience Agents (urme)                                    
        1 +# urme                                                        
        2  
        3 -OCaml TUI + MCP server for linking git history to Claude Code 
          -conversations. Browse commits, see which Claude edits explain 
          -each diff, detect human edit modifications, and search past in
          -teractions.                                                   
        3 +OCaml TUI + MCP server for linking git history to Claude Code 
          +conversations.                                                
        4 +Browse commits, see which Claude edits explain each diff, dete
          +ct human                                                      
        5 +modifications, and search past interactions.                  
        6  
        7  ## How It Works
        8  
        7 -Every time you save a step, the agent:                        
        8 -1. Creates a **git micro-commit** capturing the current file s
          -tate                                                          
        9 -2. Computes the **diff** and list of changed files            
       10 -3. Stores the full **conversation transcript**, intent, and me
          -tadata in ChromaDB (vector DB)                                
       11 -4. Indexes by both intent and conversation for **three-stage s
          -emantic search**                                              
        9 +urme V2 is a single-binary tool backed by a local SQLite store
       10 +(`.urme/db.sqlite` at the project root). There are no external
          + services вҖ”                                                   
       11 +no ChromaDB, no Ollama, no vector embeddings.                 
       12  
       13 -This means Claude can later search for similar past work, repl
          -ay step-by-step solutions, or semantically undo to a previous 
          -state.                                                        
       13 +1. **Indexing**: reads the Claude Code session logs under     
       14 +   `~/.claude/projects/<encoded-project-path>/*.jsonl` and wri
          +tes one                                                       
       15 +   `steps` row per turn, with deterministic metadata (files to
          +uched,                                                        
       16 +   commands run, tokens, git commit_before/after).            
       17 +2. **Summarisation**: runs the `claude` CLI (Haiku 4.5, one sp
          +awn per                                                       
       18 +   batch of 8 turns) to produce a one-sentence summary + 3вҖ“8 t
          +ags for                                                       
       19 +   each step. Written back into the step row; FTS5 indexes the
          +m                                                             
       20 +   automatically.                                             
       21 +3. **Git linkage**: runs the branch-aware `Git_walk` algorithm
          + against                                                      
       22 +   the Edit/Write tool_use history and populates the `edit_lin
          +ks` table                                                     
       23 +   with per-edit вҶ’ commit linkage. Human edits (content in a c
          +ommit                                                         
       24 +   that no Claude edit explains) are detected by reconciliatio
          +n.                                                            
       25 +4. **Search**: FTS5 + BM25 over `summary`, `tags`, `prompt_tex
          +t`.                                                           
       26 +   Optional `--smart` mode has Claude rewrite sparse queries a
          +nd                                                            
       27 +   rerank the shortlist with a one-sentence synthesis answer. 
       28  
       29 +Claude access goes exclusively through the `claude` CLI subpro
          +cess вҖ” no                                                     
       30 +`ANTHROPIC_API_KEY`, no direct API calls. Uses your Max subscr
          +iption.                                                       
       31 +

      108 -In auto-recording mode:

          -the full transcript                                           
      110 -- If you say **yes** or continue working, the step is kept

          -ct_step` to undo the last step (rolls back git + removes from 
          -vector DB)                                                    
      112 -- When you're done, say `save experience` to finalize вҖ” this s
          -quashes all micro-commits into one clean commit and saves the 
          -group as a single searchable entity

          -er group immediately

вҸә Runtime bug. Git_index.update uses Domainslib (spawns domains), then
  Prompts.ask tries to Lwt_process.open_process_full which uses Unix.fork вҖ” and
  OCaml 5 forbids fork after Domain.spawn. Two fixes:

  1. Short-term: reorder init so summarisation runs before the git linker (which
   uses domains).
  2. Proper fix: change Process.spawn_oneshot to use Unix.create_process
  (posix_spawn, domain-safe) like lib/git/ops.ml already does.

  Doing #1 first so the user is unblocked, then #2.

  вҺҝ В test_indexer: test_indexer: OK

вҸә All green. Now your git concern вҖ” "the git is not great". Can you tell me more
   about what you're seeing?

  Possible causes after my surgery:
  - Coverage shrinkage: the in-TUI Git browser used to load per-edit git_links
  from ChromaDB; now they come from the edit_links table, which only gets
  populated after urme init runs the walker. If your init crashed mid-way (the
  fork-after-domain error), the edit_links table may be empty or partial.
  - Link-count drop: the new linker ran after summarise in my reordered init,
  but summarise crashed before вҖ” so the walker never ran at all. Explains an
  empty Git browser.
  - Ordering bug in new init: I moved summarise before linking; if summarise
  itself fails, linking never runs.

  What are you seeing specifically вҖ” empty branch list, no link counts, wrong
  colors, something else? A screenshot or the exact status message would help me
   pinpoint it.

  Meanwhile you can rerun init cleanly now that fork-after-domain is fixed:

  dune exec bin/main.exe -- init --skip-summaries

  That skips the (already-done) summaries and just runs the walker, populating
  edit_links against your existing SQLite store.

вң» SautГ©ed for 12m 51s

вқҜ I see si i first run init when I start? and then what do i do?                

вҸә Workflow in one list:

  First time in a project:
  urme --project-dir . init
  This populates .urme/db.sqlite with:
  - all session turns from ~/.claude/projects/...
  - summaries + tags (Haiku one-shot per batch of 8)
  - per-edit git linkage (the walker)

  Takes a while (100s per 50-60 turns for the Haiku pass). Safe to re-run вҖ” it's
   idempotent: step rows without summaries get filled, rows with summaries are
  skipped, edit_links get upserted.

  Daily use вҖ” just launch the TUI:
  urme --project-dir .
  No init needed again unless you want to pull in new session JSONL. The TUI
  does:
  - History pane вҖ” list sessions, browse turns, type / to search (FTS5).
  - Git pane вҖ” browse branches/commits/files with per-edit Claude-edit
  attribution, blue for human-edited files.
  - Press i inside History to wipe the DB and re-init from scratch.

  Ad-hoc queries from the shell:
  urme search "query"           # fast (FTS5 only)
  urme search "query" --smart   # Claude rewrite + rerank with synthesis

  MCP (for Claude Code to call as a tool):
  Register once:
  claude mcp add -s user experience /path/to/bin/experience-agent --
  --project-dir .
  Then inside any Claude Code session, Claude can invoke search_history,
  file_history, region_blame, explain_change, commit_links, search_by_file. No
  manual launch вҖ” Claude Code spawns urme serve on demand.

  When you have new Claude sessions (e.g. after a week of coding):
  urme --project-dir . init
  Re-index. Picks up only the new turns because it detects existing session_id
  rows.

  Short version: init once per project (or when you want fresh sessions); then 
  urme opens the TUI; urme search for quick CLI lookups.

вҸә Bad news and good news.

  Bad: 3 done out of 463. The indexer just wiped the 365 summaries we had вҖ”
  because Indexer.index_session does clear_session_steps + reinsert, treating
  each re-index as a full rewrite of that session's rows. The summaries got
  deleted along with the rows they were attached to. That's a real bug in the
  idempotency model.

  Good: Haiku is much faster than what we were seeing before with Sonnet, so the
   re-run should be ~15вҖ“30 min for 460 turns (previously ~60 min with Sonnet for
   391).

  Options:

  1. Let it keep running. It'll rebuild all 463 summaries on Haiku. ~20 min-ish.
  2. Stop it now and restore the snapshot at /tmp/urme-snap-*.sqlite (237
  summaries from an earlier export). Then run init again вҖ” it'll only summarise
  what's missing (226). ~10 min.
  3. Stop and fix the indexer first to be properly idempotent (upsert by
  (session_id, turn_index), preserve summaries), then re-run. ~5 min to write
  the fix, then re-summarise from zero (since summaries are already gone).

  My recommendation: option 2 (restore snapshot, rerun with fix) вҖ” cheapest
  total time and stops the bleeding. But to do that I need to also fix the
  indexer bug first, or re-running init will wipe the restored summaries again.

  Cleanest: fix the indexer bug first, stop the current init, restore snapshot,
  then re-run. I can do the fix in ~2 min вҖ” want me to?

вқҜ it must be stuck or something 

вҸә Not stuck вҖ” just slower than you hoped. In the 20s between my two checks it
  went from 11 вҶ’ 19 (1 batch of 8). That's a consistent ~24 turns/min, so:

  - 463 - 19 = 444 remaining
  - ~55 more batches Г— ~20s = ~18 min to go

  Where the time goes: not Haiku inference (that's fast, ~2s for 8 turns). It's
  the Claude CLI cold-start вҖ” every batch spawns a fresh claude subprocess which
   takes ~10вҖ“15s before it even starts inferring. 8 turns Г— tiny Haiku output
  fits inside that startup cost.

  Ways to make it faster (require restart):
  1. Increase batch size 8 вҶ’ 20 or 24: ~в…“ the spawns, ~в…“ the time.
  2. Parallel spawns: run 2вҖ“3 claude CLIs at once. Needs Lwt concurrency.
  3. Persistent daemon mode: spawn once, send N prompts down stdin. Biggest
  speedup but requires restoring the daemon code I just deleted.

  Honestly just let it finish вҖ” 18 min is the reality with Claude CLI's
  cold-start tax, and you're already halfway to having all 463 turns done. Once
  we're there, the next re-run only touches new turns (after I fix the clobber
  bug), which is seconds.

  Shall I (a) just wait, (b) bump batch size to 20 before the next run, or (c)
  also fix the index_session clobber bug right now so the next init preserves
  summaries?

          +cr out_rd) in

      175 +

      177 +  let rec reader () =                                         
      178 +    let* line_opt = Lwt.catch                                 
      179 +      (fun () -> Lwt_io.read_line_opt out_ic)                 
      180 +      (fun _ -> Lwt.return_none) in                           
      181 +    match line_opt with                                       
      182 +    | Some line ->                                            
      183 +      (match Stream.parse_line line with                      
      184 +       | Some event -> push (Some event)                      
      185 +       | None -> ());                                         
      186 +      reader ()                                               
      187 +    | None -> push None; Lwt.return_unit                      
      188 +  in                                                          
      189 +  Lwt.async reader;                                           
      190 +  Lwt.return { daemon_pid = pid; daemon_stdin = stdin_chan;   
      191 +               daemon_events = events }                       
      192 +                                                              
      193 +(* Send one prompt down the daemon's stdin, read events until 
          +the next                                                      
      194 +   [Result] marker, return the accumulated assistant text.    
      195 +                                                              
      196 +   Assumes the caller serialises ask calls on a single daemon 
          +вҖ” two                                                         
      197 +   concurrent asks would interleave event streams and garbage 
          +the                                                           
      198 +   output boundary. The pool in [prompts.ml] enforces this. *)
      199 +let ask_daemon d ~prompt =                                    
      200 +  let line =                                                  
      201 +    let json = `Assoc [                                       
      202 +      "type", `String "user";                                 
      203 +      "message", `Assoc [                                     
      204 +        "role", `String "user";                               
      205 +        "content", `String prompt;                            
      206 +      ];                                                      
      207 +    ] in                                                      
      208 +    Yojson.Safe.to_string json ^ "\n"                         
      209 +  in                                                          
      210 +  let* () = Lwt_io.write d.daemon_stdin line in               
      211 +  let* () = Lwt_io.flush d.daemon_stdin in                    
      212 +  let buf = Buffer.create 1024 in                             
      213 +  let rec loop () =                                           
      214 +    let* ev = Lwt_stream.get d.daemon_events in               
      215 +    match ev with                                             
      216 +    | Some (Stream.Assistant_message { content; _ }) ->       
      217 +      Buffer.add_string buf (Stream.text_of_content content); 
      218 +      loop ()                                                 
      219 +    | Some (Stream.Result _) ->                               
      220 +      Lwt.return (Buffer.contents buf)                        
      221 +    | Some _ -> loop ()                                       
      222 +    | None -> Lwt.return (Buffer.contents buf)                
      223 +  in                                                          
      224 +  loop ()                                                     
      225 +                                                              
      226 +let close_daemon d =                                          
      227 +  let* () = Lwt.catch (fun () -> Lwt_io.close d.daemon_stdin) 
      228 +    (fun _ -> Lwt.return_unit) in                             
      229 +  let* _pid, status = Lwt_unix.waitpid [] d.daemon_pid in     
      230 +  Lwt.return status

      55 +(* ---------- Daemon pool for high-volume batching ---------- *
         +)                                                              
      56 +                                                               
      57 +(* A pool of K persistent claude daemons, each dispatched seria
         +lly.                                                           
      58 +   Use [with_pool] to spin up, distribute work, and tear down. 
         +*)                                                             
      59 +                                                               
      60 +type pool = {                                                  
      61 +  daemons  : Process.daemon list;                              
      62 +  queue    : Process.daemon Lwt_mvar.t;  (* acts as a semaphore
         + *)                                                            
      63 +}                                                              
      64 +                                                               
      65 +let spawn_pool ?model ?(size=3) ~binary () =                   
      66 +  let opts = { Process.default_opts with model; allowed_tools =
         + [] } in                                                       
      67 +  let* daemons = Lwt_list.map_s (fun _ ->                      
      68 +    Process.spawn_daemon ~cwd:"." ~opts ~binary ()             
      69 +  ) (List.init size (fun _ -> ())) in                          
      70 +  let queue = Lwt_mvar.create_empty () in                      
      71 +  let* () = Lwt_list.iter_s (Lwt_mvar.put queue) daemons in    
      72 +  Lwt.return { daemons; queue }                                
      73 +                                                               
      74 +let with_daemon pool f =                                       
      75 +  let* d = Lwt_mvar.take pool.queue in                         
      76 +  Lwt.finalize                                                 
      77 +    (fun () -> f d)                                            
      78 +    (fun () -> Lwt_mvar.put pool.queue d)                      
      79 +                                                               
      80 +let close_pool pool =                                          
      81 +  Lwt_list.iter_s (fun d ->                                    
      82 +    let* _ = Process.close_daemon d in Lwt.return_unit         
      83 +  ) pool.daemons                                               
      84 +                                                               
      85 +(* Pool-aware ask: checks out a daemon, sends the prompt, relea
         +ses. *)                                                        
      86 +let ask_via_pool pool ~prompt =                                
      87 +  with_daemon pool (fun d ->                                   
      88 +    let* raw = Process.ask_daemon d ~prompt in                 
      89 +    Lwt.return (strip_fences raw))

  building per-edit git links...

  You get a batch i/total done line per batch completion вҖ” because they run in
  parallel the numbers won't arrive in order, but !done_ increments
  monotonically so the i/total always reflects progress.

  in.

   just sits there. Once it completes (or you kill it), the new output kicks in.

вҸә It's working, just slow вҖ” each batch was completing in ~15s. The problem is
  that claude --print --input-format stream-json re-initialises its session per 
  prompt (notice the System_init event at the start of each batch, not just
  batch #1). It's not a true daemon вҖ” each prompt pays the full ~5-10s CLI
  startup tax.

  Good news: with pool=3 (parallel daemons), 100 batches becomes ~33 per daemon
  Г— 15s вүҲ 8 min. And with your DB wiped to 0 summaries, the re-run will also
  cover what's missing.

  My non-blocking-fd fix still applies вҖ” though it wasn't the actual blocker, it
   will make Lwt scheduling more responsive.

  Let me clean up the verbose debug prints (keep the batch-completion lines,
  drop the per-event traces) and bump back to pool=3.

вҸә Update(lib/engine/summarise.ml)
  вҺҝ В User rejected update to lib/engine/summarise.ml

вқҜ so is there a way to not pay this? can I run a proper daemon?                 

вҸә Let me give you the honest picture first, because "daemon" has two meanings
  and only one of them saves time.

  What the Claude CLI actually does with --input-format stream-json:

  The same process handles many prompts over its lifetime (that part works). But
   every prompt triggers a fresh System_init вҖ” meaning the CLI rebuilds its
  internal state (tool registry, prompt cache, model config) per prompt. Each
  System_init re-creates the ~32K-token prompt cache (you can see
  cache_creation_input_tokens: 31982 in the earlier Result event). So we're
  paying ~32K input tokens of cache setup on every call.

  Where the 15s-per-batch actually goes:
  1. ~1вҖ“3s: CLI/startup per prompt (cache rebuild, tool registry init)
  2. ~8вҖ“12s: Haiku inference on a 3вҖ“5KB prompt + API round-trip
  3. Small overhead

  So the "tax" isn't really the process startup вҖ” it's Haiku doing real work on
  real-sized prompts and rebuilding its cache each time.

  Can we skip the cache rebuild? Yes, if the CLI can share its cache across
  prompts in one session. Let me check what flags exist.

вҸә Bash(claude --help 2>&1 | head -80)
  вҺҝ В Usage: claude [options] [command] [prompt]

     Claude Code - starts an interactive session by default, use -p/--print
     вҖҰ +129 lines (ctrl+o to expand)

вҸә Found the real fix. The tax isn't the daemon protocol вҖ” it's that Claude CLI
  in default mode rebuilds a 32K-token prompt cache on every call (tool
  definitions, CLAUDE.md discovery, memory paths, agents, plugins, MCP server
  specs, LSPвҖҰ). For summarisation we need exactly none of that.

  Two flags make this go away:

  - --bare вҖ” "Minimal mode: skip hooks, LSP, plugin sync, attribution,
  auto-memory, background prefetches, keychain reads, CLAUDE.md auto-discovery."
   Kills almost the entire system-prompt bloat.
  - Custom --system-prompt вҖ” replaces the default 32K-token system prompt with
  our own ~200-token instruction.

  Let me wire it.

вҸә All green. Summary of what's different now:

  - --bare on every daemon: skips hooks, LSP, plugin sync, auto-memory,
  CLAUDE.md discovery, attribution. This alone should cut the per-prompt cache
  from ~32K to ~1K tokens.
  - --tools "": no tool registry.
  - Custom --system-prompt: the summarisation instruction is now a cacheable
  constant, not part of each user prompt. Each user prompt shrinks by ~300
  tokens.
  - Pool = 3 daemons in parallel.
  - Non-blocking fds on all parent-side pipes (from the earlier debug).

  Expected result per batch: probably 3-5s instead of 15s. 100 batches / 3
  daemons Г— 3s вүҲ ~100s = under 2 minutes.

  Kill any hanging daemons and rerun:

  pkill -f "claude-haiku-4-5"; dune exec bin/main.exe -- init

вҸә Found it вҖ” my bug. Lwt_mvar.create_empty is a single-slot mvar, so the first
  Lwt_mvar.put daemon1 succeeds, but put daemon2 blocks forever waiting for
  someone to take. That's why we stop right before "queue populated". Swapping
  to Lwt_pool, which is actually designed for this.

вҸә Found it вҖ” --bare is incompatible with your Max subscription. From the help
  text: "Anthropic auth is strictly ANTHROPIC_API_KEY or apiKeyHelper via 
  --settings (OAuth and keychain are never read)". Our clean_env strips
  ANTHROPIC_API_KEY, so --bare daemons have no auth path вҶ’ they return "Not
  logged in" instead of real responses. The 35 summaries that landed were
  probably from daemons that had cached state from a prior non-bare run.

  Dropping --bare. We keep --tools "" and the custom --system-prompt (both fine
  with OAuth) and the 3-daemon pool. Per-batch latency goes back up a bit (~10s
  instead of ~3s) because of the tool-registry rebuild, but still 3Г— faster than
   serial.

  в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

  Why so few sessions produce edits: out of 88 Claude Code sessions, 85 are
  text-only (no Edit/Write tool_use blocks) вҖ” just chat. Only 3 sessions
  actually authored code, which is consistent with this repo's history (the big
  Mar-16 session + Mar-30 session + the current v2 session).

  Why 318 orphans: these are edits whose content doesn't match any diff on the
  current branches вҖ” usually because the file got subsequently rewritten, or the
   edit was on a throwaway file that never got committed. The walker's
  reconciliation is strict (exact substring match), so any "soft" changes
  (reformatting, later Write that replaced the file) leave the earlier Edit
  orphaned.

  What the TUI uses: it groups by (commit_sha, file_base). 29 commits Г— ~1-2
  files each вҶ’ 37 groups. That's the number you see.

  So the coverage is actually reasonable вҖ” 131/317 Claude edits linked = 41%,
  which for strict-substring reconciliation across hundreds of rewrites isn't
  bad. If you want more coverage, it'd need fuzzier matching (diff-hash or
  line-similarity), which is a different algorithm.

  Want to leave it as-is and call task #9 + the wean-off complete, or poke at
  the orphan rate?

вҸә Actually those search results reveal a separate, bigger bug вҖ” the summariser's
   own prompts are being re-indexed. Look at the top hits: they all start with
  Input turns: --- turn 0 --- User: You summarise turns from a Claude Code 
  coding session... вҖ” that's the text WE send to Claude when we summarise, being
   logged by the Claude CLI, then picked up by urme init on the next run.

  Two things going on:

  1. Your "move to nottui" commit has no JSONL вҖ” nothing was indexed for Mar 26.
   Either that session happened before you started using urme, was done via
  Claude.ai web, or the JSONL file got deleted from ~/.claude/projects/. The
  walker correctly attributed those changes to "human" because no Claude edit
  explains them. That's not a bug; it's honest.

  2. Summariser prompts polluting the index вҖ” every time urme summarises, those
  3 parallel daemons each create a session JSONL in ~/.claude/projects/вҖҰ/. Next
  urme init picks them up and indexes them, and the next summarise pass
  re-summarises them (notice the recursive Input turns: --- turn 0 --- User: 
  Input turns: --- turn 0 --- User: ... prefixes вҖ” that's
  summaries-of-summaries).

  Fix: pass --no-session-persistence to the summariser's claude CLI. Then its
  sessions never hit disk and never contaminate the index.

вқҜ why can't I run urme --init -j 8?                                             

вҸә Subcommand vs flag вҖ” init is a subcommand, not a flag, so no -- prefix. Plus
  -j 8 needs to come after the subcommand (it's a subcommand-specific flag).

  Correct:
  urme init -j 8
  urme init --parallel 8
  urme init -j 8 --project-dir .

  What you typed (urme --init -j 8) would be parsed as: try to use --init as a
  global flag (doesn't exist), fallback to the default subcommand (TUI), with -j
   8 passed to that (which also doesn't have -j).

  If you're running from the source repo rather than an installed urme:
  dune exec bin/main.exe -- init -j 8
  The -- there separates dune's own args from the program's args.

  about right for how much of a conversation is actually authoring code vs
  discussion/planning.

  No more recursive summariser noise, no Chroma, no fork-after-domain crashes,
  no EINTR. Wean-off is done.

вқҜ which is as stupid 

вҸә Right вҖ” your state is back to 286/292 linked on main (the good numbers), so
  the walker works. Your complaint is the persistent "human" classification on 
  files you know were Claude-edited.

  Fundamental issue: the walker's algorithm is "any byte of committed content 
  that my replay of Claude's edits doesn't reproduce = human edit". It's a
  strict substring-reconciliation. If a single character differs вҖ” trailing
  whitespace, CRLF/LF, an import Claude added that you tweaked, a pre-commit
  hook running a formatter, a Write that captures 90% of the final file вҖ” the
  walker spawns a "human" link for the diff.

  When you see "human followed by Claude Edit" on branch_diff.ml, the Claude
  part is real (walker matched turn 137 of session 03944e26). The "human" part
  represents content in the committed file that didn't exactly match what 
  Claude's edits would produce, not "you typed it by hand."

  The algorithm just can't distinguish:
  - "Claude really missed this part вҖ” user typed it"
  - "Claude did it but a post-hook / formatter / CRLF changed some bytes"
  - "Claude did it in a session we don't have the JSONL for"

  All three show up identically as human:.

  Three options (in rough effort order):

  - (a) Relabel: drop "human" in the UI and call it unmatched or unknown. Tells
  you "walker couldn't attribute this" without implying you typed it. ~10 min.
  - (b) Collapse "human" into adjacent Claude links: if a Claude edit exists on
  the same (commit, file), suppress the human sibling and just attribute the
  whole change to Claude. Loses the "something diverged" signal but cleaner UI.
  ~30 min.
  - (c) Line-level fuzzy matching: rewrite the walker's reconciler to work on
  lines, not bytes, and ignore whitespace-only diffs. Much more robust but real
  work. ~few hours.

  Which?

вҸә Found it. The numbers match perfectly:
  - Claude Write: 3796 bytes
  - Claude Edit: 492B вҶ’ 621B (net +129)
  - 3796 + 129 = 3925 bytes вҖ” exactly the current file size

  So there's literally no missing content вҖ” everything in branch_diff.ml came
  from those two Claude tool_uses. The walker is creating a bogus "human" edit,
  most likely because the Patch library's diff+patch roundtrip is not byte-exact
   (trailing newlines, context-line handling, etc.), so the walker's
  materialised state differs from the committed content even though logically
  they should match.

  Read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

вҸә You're right to be pissed. The walker's storing patches (via OCaml's Patch
  library) and then replaying them against the git blob to compare вҖ” which means
   it's subject to Patch.diff+Patch.patch round-trip quirks (trailing newlines,
  EOL handling, context line fuzziness). For a file where the whole content
  demonstrably came from two Claude tool_uses, getting a "human" at all means
  the patch library isn't byte-exact.

  The right fix is to drop the Patch library entirely and track state as the 
  direct string. For each edit:
  - Write: state = the Write's content verbatim.
  - Edit: state = splice(state, old_string вҶ’ new_string).

  Then compare state == blob, byte for byte. No round-trip, no artifacts.

  That's maybe ~40 min of rewrite. Alternatively, a quick stopgap: skip
  generating a human edit when the diff between walker-state and commit is
  trivially small (whitespace-only, trailing newline). That hides the noise but
  doesn't fix the underlying fragility.

  Both, neither, or just live with it for now and call task #9 honestly done
  (the wean-off is complete, the walker precision gripe is a pre-existing
  algorithmic limitation)? Your call.

вқҜ what human reconciliation? wtf are you talking about 

вҸә Sorry вҖ” "human reconciliation" is my jargon. Plainly:

  The walker tracks what file contents SHOULD be based on Claude's edits, then
  at each commit compares to what's actually in git. Any mismatch вҶ’ walker
  creates a synthetic "human edit" labeled with the diff, to represent "bytes in
   the commit that my Claude replay doesn't explain." Label's a misnomer вҖ” it
  can be a hook, a formatter, a missing JSONL, OR a bug in the walker's replay
  logic. In your branch_diff.ml case it's the last one.

  The specific bug I just found:

  git_walk.ml has a file_state type with a Created variant that exists but is 
  never used. The Write path stores state as Patches regardless of whether the
  file is new or pre-existing. When the walker later materialises a
  Write-created file:

  1. It reads the blob at last_commit (the PREVIOUS commit, before the Write).
  2. For a newly-created file, that read returns None (file didn't exist).
  3. It tries to apply the Write's patch to None base via Patch.patch 
  ~cleanly:false None p вҖ” which very likely returns None.
  4. materialise returns None, walker sees "expected empty / actual 3925B" вҶ’
  spurious human edit for the whole file.

  That's specifically an artifact of how I'm calling the Patch library (None
  base), not a bug in the library itself. Let me fix it.

вқҜ it is just that a write step will not have any "before" now? it is not an edit 

вҸә Yes вҖ” you've nailed it. A Write has no "before" to diff against; it just sets
  the file's content. The walker is manufacturing a fake before/after patch pair
   (via Patch.diff) for what's logically a pure "set contents = this". The
  round-trip through the Patch library then can lose bytes.

  Fix: for Write (and subsequent Edits after a Write), track the file as a
  direct string, not a Patch chain. I'll add a Content of string variant.

вң» Churned for 35s

вқҜ [materialise] file=/Users/corneliuhoffman/Documents/experience-agent/lib/engi 
  ne/branch_diff.ml commit=b370fda npatches=0 base=None result=None             
  [materialise] file=lib/engine/branch_diff.ml commit=b370fda npatches=0        
  base=None result=None                                                         
  [reconcile] lib/engine/branch_diff.ml at ts=1776773365 (last_commit=b370fda)  
    expected_s len=0 (materialise=None)                                         
    actual_s   len=3925                                                         
    actual longer by 3925 bytes, tail="(* Diff saved git state against current  
  git state to determi"                                                         
    patches on file before: 0                                                   

вҸә Found it! patches on file before: 0 вҖ” the walker has zero patches for
  branch_diff.ml when it reconciles against the commit. The Claude Write/Edit
  were never applied.

  Root cause: the walker processes each branch independently, re-walking all
  reachable commits. The Claude edits on branch_diff.ml are tagged with
  git_branch="v2". But if the walker hits ead1c42 on a DIFFERENT branch's walk
  first (e.g. main, where the edits don't apply because the filter drops them),
  it processes the commit with patches=0 вҶ’ spurious human edit is written. Then
  when it later walks v2 with the edits, the Claude Write+Edit get saved, but
  the human row from the earlier walk is already in the DB.

  So the DB ends up with both a "human" and a "claude" link for the same file at
   the same commit. The walker's algorithm is correct per-branch; the bug is
  that it writes the same commit twice across branches.

  Cheap pragmatic fix: in load_git_links_from_db, suppress human rows when a
  Claude row exists for the same (commit_sha, file_base). Preserves the
  "genuinely unexplained" human edits but hides the branch-walk artifacts.

вқҜ the human part looks shite ... if there are no claude ones it should be

вҸә Right вҖ” for a pure-human commit (no Claude at same commit/file), the
  old_content we store is the walker's "expected" (often empty), not the actual
  parent blob. So the "diff" we render looks like "whole file was created" not
  like the real commit's diff.

  Fix: pass the commit's before content into reconcile and store that as
  old_string on the human edit. Then the rendered diff is the actual parent вҶ’ 
  commit delta.

вҸә Bash(# Dump one human row's old/new content to tmp and diff with real git diff
      sqlite3 .urme/db.sqlite <<'SQL' > /tmp/dm.tsvвҖҰ)
  вҺҝ В      285 /tmp/old.ml
